<li><a href="/wiki/2019_Turkish_offensive_into_north-eastern_Syria" title="2019 Turkish offensive into north-eastern Syria">2019 Turkish offensive into north-eastern Syria</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Israel_and_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Israel and the Syrian civil war">Israel's role</a></li></ul>
<p><b>U.S.-led intervention against ISIL</b>
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/US_intervention_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="US intervention in the Syrian civil war">US intervention</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Timeline_of_US_intervention_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Timeline of US intervention in the Syrian civil war">Timeline</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/List_of_United_States_attacks_on_Syria_during_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="List of United States attacks on Syria during the Syrian civil war">List of attacks</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2014_American_rescue_mission_in_Syria" title="2014 American rescue mission in Syria">2014 rescue operation</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/May_2015_U.S._special_forces_raid_in_Syria" title="May 2015 U.S. special forces raid in Syria">May 2015 raid</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/2017_Shayrat_missile_strike" title="2017 Shayrat missile strike">2017 missile strikes</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Qatari_involvement_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Qatari involvement in the Syrian civil war">Qatari involvement</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Jordanian_intervention_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Jordanian intervention in the Syrian civil war">Jordanian intervention</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Martyr_Muath" title="Operation Martyr Muath">Operation Martyr Muath</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lebanon%27s_role_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" class="mw-redirect" title="Lebanon&#39;s role in the Syrian civil war">Lebanon's role</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Saudi_involvement_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Saudi involvement in the Syrian civil war">Saudi involvement</a>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/April_2018_missile_strikes_against_Syria" title="April 2018 missile strikes against Syria">April 2018 missile strikes</a></li></ul></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dutch_involvement_in_the_Syrian_civil_war" title="Dutch involvement in the Syrian civil war">Dutch involvement</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/German_intervention_against_the_Islamic_State" title="German intervention against the Islamic State">German intervention</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Op%C3%A9ration_Chammal" title="Opération Chammal">French intervention</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Okra" title="Operation Okra">Australian intervention</a></li>
<li><a href="/wiki/Operation_Shader" title="Operation Shader">UK intervention</a></li></ul></div></td></tr></tbody></table><div></div></td></tr></tbody></table></div>
<p>The <b>Syrian Electronic Army</b> (<b>SEA</b>; <a href="/wiki/Arabic_language" class="mw-redirect" title="Arabic language">Arabic</a>: <span lang="ar" dir="rtl">الجيش السوري الإلكتروني</span>) is a group of <a href="/wiki/Hacker_(computer_security)" class="mw-redirect" title="Hacker (computer security)">computer hackers</a> which first surfaced online in 2011 to support the government of <a href="/wiki/Syria" title="Syria">Syrian</a> President <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a>. Using <a href="/wiki/Spamming" title="Spamming">spamming</a>, <a href="/wiki/Website_defacement" title="Website defacement">website defacement</a>, <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a>, <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">phishing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Denial-of-service_attack" title="Denial-of-service attack">denial-of-service attacks</a>, it has targeted terrorist organizations, political opposition groups, western news outlets, human rights groups and websites that are seemingly neutral to the Syrian conflict. It has also hacked government websites in the <a href="/wiki/Middle_East" title="Middle East">Middle East</a> and Europe, as well as US defense contractors. As of 2011<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup>, the SEA has been "the first Arab country to have a public Internet Army hosted on its national networks to openly launch <a href="/wiki/Cyberwarfare" title="Cyberwarfare">cyber attacks</a> on its enemies".<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>The precise nature of SEA's relationship with the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_government" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian government">Syrian government</a> has changed over time and is unclear.<sup id="cite_ref-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-3"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>3<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<meta property="mw:PageProp/toc" />
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Origins_and_historical_context">Origins and historical context</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Origins and historical context"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>In the 1990s, Syrian President <a href="/wiki/Bashar_al-Assad" title="Bashar al-Assad">Bashar al-Assad</a> headed the <a href="/wiki/Syrian_Computer_Society" title="Syrian Computer Society">Syrian Computer Society</a>, which is connected to the SEA, according to research by University of Toronto and University of Cambridge, UK.<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> There is evidence that a Syrian Malware Team goes as far back as January 1, 2011.<sup id="cite_ref-FireEye_4-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FireEye-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
In February 2011, after years of <a href="/wiki/Internet_censorship" title="Internet censorship">Internet censorship</a>, Syrian censors lifted a ban on <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> and <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In April 2011, only days after anti-regime protests escalated in Syria, Syrian Electronic Army emerged on Facebook.<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-3" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On May 5, 2011 the Syrian Computer Society registered SEA’s website (syrian-es.com).<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-4" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Because Syria's domain registration authority registered the hacker site, some security experts have written that the group was supervised by the Syrian state.<sup id="cite_ref-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-5"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>5<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> SEA claimed on its webpage to be no official entity, but "a group of enthusiastic Syrian youths who could not stay passive towards the massive distortion of facts about the recent uprising in Syria".<sup id="cite_ref-BBCFowler_6-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBCFowler-6"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>6<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> 
As soon as May 27, 2011 SEA had removed text that denied it was an official entity.<sup id="cite_ref-opennet_2-5" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-opennet-2"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>2<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> One commentator has noted that "[SEA] volunteers might include <a href="/wiki/Syrian_diaspora" title="Syrian diaspora">Syrian diaspora</a>; some of their hacks have used <a href="/wiki/Colloquial_English" class="mw-redirect" title="Colloquial English">colloquial English</a> and <a href="/wiki/Reddit" title="Reddit">Reddit</a> memes.<sup id="cite_ref-POST_7-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POST-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> In July 2011, it emerged that Bashar al-Assad's page on Facebook page was run by a member of the Syrian Electronic Army close to the regime, Haidara Suleiman, the son of powerful intelligence officer and former Syrian ambassador in Amman, <a href="/wiki/Bahjat_Suleiman" title="Bahjat Suleiman">Bahjat Suleiman</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> He told AFP that "the official media is unfortunately weak... This is why we use electronic media to show people what's going on."<sup id="cite_ref-:0_8-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-8"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>8<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p><p>According to a 2014 report by security company Intelcrawler, SEA activity has shown links with "officials in Syria, Iran, Lebanon and Hezbollah."<sup id="cite_ref-Robertson24032014_9-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Robertson24032014-9"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>9<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> A February 2015 article by <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> stated that "American intelligence officials" suspect the SEA is "actually Iranian".<sup id="cite_ref-NYT2215_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-NYT2215-10"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>10<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> However, no data has shown a link between Iran's and Syria's cyber attack patterns according to an analysis of "<a href="/wiki/Open-source_intelligence" title="Open-source intelligence">open-source intelligence</a>" by cyber security firm <a href="/wiki/Recorded_Future" title="Recorded Future">Recorded Future</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-kingWSJ9513_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-kingWSJ9513-11"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>11<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Online_activities">Online activities</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Online activities"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>SEA has pursued activities in three key areas:
</p>
<ul><li><a href="/wiki/Website_defacement" title="Website defacement">Website defacement</a> and electronic surveillance against <a href="/wiki/Syrian_rebels" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian rebels">Syrian rebels</a> and other opposition: The SEA has carried out surveillance to discover the identities and location of <a href="/wiki/Syrian_rebels" class="mw-redirect" title="Syrian rebels">Syrian rebels</a>, using <a href="/wiki/Malware" title="Malware">malware</a> (including the <a href="/wiki/Blackworm" title="Blackworm">Blackworm</a> tool),<sup id="cite_ref-FireEye_4-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-FireEye-4"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>4<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">phishing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Denial_of_service_attacks" class="mw-redirect" title="Denial of service attacks">denial of service attacks</a>. As of 2013<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit">&#91;update&#93;</a></sup> this electronic monitoring has extended to foreign aid workers.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>12<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Defacement attacks against Western websites that it contends spread news hostile to the Syrian government: These have included news websites such as <a href="/wiki/BBC_News" title="BBC News">BBC News</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a>, <a href="/wiki/National_Public_Radio" class="mw-redirect" title="National Public Radio">National Public Radio</a>, <a href="/wiki/CBC_News" title="CBC News">CBC News</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-13" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>13<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network" title="Al Jazeera Media Network">Al Jazeera</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Financial_Times" title="Financial Times">Financial Times</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>14<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/The_Washington_Post" title="The Washington Post">The Washington Post</a></i>,<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>15<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> Syrian satellite broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Orient_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Orient TV">Orient TV</a>, and Dubai-based <a href="/wiki/Al-Arabia_TV" class="mw-redirect" title="Al-Arabia TV">al-Arabia TV</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-Opennet1_16-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Opennet1-16"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>16<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> as well as rights organizations such as <a href="/wiki/Human_Rights_Watch" title="Human Rights Watch">Human Rights Watch</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>17<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> SEA targets include <a href="/wiki/VoIP" class="mw-redirect" title="VoIP">VoIP</a> apps, such as <a href="/wiki/Viber" title="Viber">Viber</a><sup id="cite_ref-JordanCrook_18-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JordanCrook-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> and <a href="/wiki/Tango_(software)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tango (software)">Tango</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-19" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>19<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Spamming popular Facebook pages with pro-regime comments:<sup id="cite_ref-20" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>20<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The Facebook pages of President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> and former French President <a href="/wiki/Nicolas_Sarkozy" title="Nicolas Sarkozy">Nicolas Sarkozy</a> have been targeted by such spam campaigns.<sup id="cite_ref-Fowler_21-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Fowler-21"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>21<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>Global <a href="/wiki/Cyber_espionage" class="mw-redirect" title="Cyber espionage">cyber espionage</a>: "technology and media companies, allied <a href="/wiki/Military_procurement" class="mw-redirect" title="Military procurement">military procurement</a> officers, <a href="/wiki/List_of_US_defense_contractors" class="mw-redirect" title="List of US defense contractors">US defense contractors</a>, and foreign attaches and embassies".<sup id="cite_ref-intel_22-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-intel-22"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>22<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<p>The SEA's tone and style vary from the serious and openly political to ironic statements intended as critical or pointed humor: SEA had "Exclusive: Terror is striking the #USA and #Obama is Shamelessly in Bed with Al-Qaeda" tweeted from the Twitter account of <i><a href="/wiki/60_Minutes" title="60 Minutes">60 Minutes</a></i>, and in July 2012 posted "Do you think Saudi and Qatar should keep funding armed gangs in Syria in order to topple the government? #Syria," from <a href="/wiki/Al_Jazeera_Media_Network" title="Al Jazeera Media Network">Al Jazeera</a>'s Twitter account before the message was removed. In another attack, members of SEA used the BBC Weather Channel Twitter account to post the headline, "Saudi weather station down due to head on-collision with camel."<sup id="cite_ref-dd_sea_twithack_23-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-dd_sea_twithack-23"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>23<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> After <i>Washington Post</i> reporter Max Fisher called their jokes unfunny, one hacker associated with the group told a <i><a href="/wiki/Vice_(magazine)" title="Vice (magazine)">Vice</a></i> interview 'haters gonna hate.'"<sup id="cite_ref-POST_7-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-POST-7"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>7<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Operating_system">Operating system</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Operating system"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<p>On 31 October 2014, the SEA released a <a href="/wiki/Linux_distribution" title="Linux distribution">Linux distribution</a> named SEANux.<sup id="cite_ref-24" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-24"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>24<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>25<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup>
</p>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Timeline_of_notable_attacks">Timeline of notable attacks</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Timeline of notable attacks"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2011">2011</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: 2011"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>July 2011: <a href="/wiki/University_of_California_Los_Angeles" class="mw-redirect" title="University of California Los Angeles">University of California Los Angeles</a> website defaced by SEA hacker "The Pro".<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>26<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>August 2011: <a href="/wiki/Anonymous_(hacker_group)" title="Anonymous (hacker group)">Anonymous</a>-run social networking platform <a href="/wiki/Anonplus" title="Anonplus">Anonplus</a> is defaced. <a href="/wiki/Citizen_Lab" title="Citizen Lab">Citizen Lab</a> attributes the attack to the Syrian Electronic Army.<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>27<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>September 2011: <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a> website defaced in what was called the work of a "sophisticated group or individual". The Harvard homepage was replaced with an image of Syrian president Bashar al-Assad with the message "Syrian Electronic Army Were Here".<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>28<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2012">2012</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: 2012"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>April 2012: The official blog of social media website <a href="/wiki/LinkedIn" title="LinkedIn">LinkedIn</a> was redirected to a site supporting Bashar al-Assad.<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>29<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>August 2012: The Twitter account of the <a href="/wiki/Reuters" title="Reuters">Reuters</a> news agency sent 22 tweets with false information on the conflict in Syria. The Reuters news website was compromised, and posted a false report about the conflict to a journalist's blog.<sup id="cite_ref-30" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>30<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2013">2013</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: 2013"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>20 April 2013: The Team Gamerfood homepage was defaced.<sup id="cite_ref-teamgamerfood.com_31-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-teamgamerfood.com-31"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>31<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>23 April 2013: The <a href="/wiki/Associated_Press" title="Associated Press">Associated Press</a> Twitter account falsely claimed the <a href="/wiki/White_House" title="White House">White House</a> had been bombed and President <a href="/wiki/Barack_Obama" title="Barack Obama">Barack Obama</a> injured. This led to a US$136.5 billion decline in value of the <a href="/wiki/S%26P_500" title="S&amp;P 500">S&amp;P 500</a> the same day.<sup id="cite_ref-Spillus_32-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Spillus-32"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>32<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-33" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-33"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>33<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>May 2013: The Twitter account of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Onion" title="The Onion">The Onion</a></i> was compromised by <a href="/wiki/Phishing" title="Phishing">phishing</a> Google Apps accounts of <i>The Onion</i><span class="nowrap" style="padding-left:0.1em;">&#39;</span>s employees. The platform was also used by the hackers to spread pro-Syrian tweets.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>34<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-theonion.github.io_35-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-theonion.github.io-35"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>35<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>24 May 2013: The <a href="/wiki/ITV_News_London" title="ITV News London">ITV News London</a> Twitter account was hacked.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>36<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>On 26 May 2013: the Android applications of British broadcaster <a href="/wiki/Sky_News" title="Sky News">Sky News</a> were hacked on Google Play Store.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>37<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>17 July 2013: <a href="/wiki/Truecaller" title="Truecaller">Truecaller</a> servers were hacked into by the Syrian Electronic Army.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>38<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> The group claimed on its Twitter handle to have recovered 459 GiBs of database, primarily due to an older version of WordPress installed on the servers. The hackers released <a href="/wiki/Truecaller" title="Truecaller">Truecaller</a>'s alleged database host ID, username, and password via another tweet.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>39<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup> On 18 July 2013, TrueCaller confirmed on its blog that only their website was hacked, but claimed that the attack did not disclose any passwords or credit card information.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>40<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>23 July 2013: <a href="/wiki/Viber" title="Viber">Viber</a> servers were hacked, the support website replaced with a message and a supposed screenshot of data that was obtained during the intrusion.<sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>41<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>42<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-JordanCrook_18-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-JordanCrook-18"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>18<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>15 August 2013: Advertising service <a href="/wiki/Outbrain" title="Outbrain">Outbrain</a> suffered a spearphishing attack and SEA placed redirects into the websites of The Washington Post, Time, and CNN.<sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>43<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>27 August 2013: NYTimes.com had its DNS redirected to a page that displayed the message "Hacked by SEA" and Twitter's domain registrar was changed.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>44<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>28 August 2013: Twitter's DNS registration showed the SEA as its Admin and Tech contacts, and some users reported that the site's <a href="/wiki/Cascading_Style_Sheets" class="mw-redirect" title="Cascading Style Sheets">Cascading Style Sheets</a> (CSS) had been compromised.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>45<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>29–30 August 2013: <i>The New York Times</i>, <i>The Huffington Post</i>, and Twitter were knocked down by the SEA. A person claiming to speak for the group stepped forward to tie these attacks to the increasing likelihood of U.S military action in response to al-Assad using chemical weapons. A self-described operative of the SEA told ABC News in an e-mail exchange: "When we hacked media we do not destroy the site but only publish on it if possible, or publish an article [that] contains the truth of what is happening in Syria. ... So if the USA launch attack on Syria we may use methods of causing harm, both for the U.S. economy or other."<sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>46<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>2–3 September 2013: Pro-Syria hackers broke into the Internet recruiting site for the <a href="/wiki/US_Marine_Corps" class="mw-redirect" title="US Marine Corps">US Marine Corps</a>, posting a message that urged US soldiers to refuse orders if Washington decides to launch a strike against the Syrian government. The site, www.marines.com, was paralyzed for several hours and redirected to a seven-sentence message "delivered by SEA".<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>47<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>30 September 2013: The <a href="/wiki/Global_Post" class="mw-redirect" title="Global Post">Global Post</a>'s official Twitter account and website were hacked. SEA posted through their Twitter account,  "Think twice before you publish untrusted informations <i>[sic]</i> about Syrian Electronic Army" and "This time we hacked your website and your Twitter account, the next time you will start searching for new job"<sup id="cite_ref-48" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-48"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>48<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>28 October 2013: By gaining access to the Gmail account of an <a href="/wiki/Organizing_for_Action" title="Organizing for Action">Organizing for Action</a> staffer, the SEA altered shortened URLs on President Obama's Facebook and Twitter accounts to point to a 24-minute pro-government video on <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>49<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>9 November 2013: SEA hacked the website of VICE, a no-affiliate news/documentary/blog website, which has filmed numerous times in Syria with the side of the Rebel forces. Logging into vice.com redirected to what appeared to be the SEA home page.<sup id="cite_ref-50" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-50"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>50<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>12 November 2013: SEA hacked the Facebook page of <a href="/wiki/Matthew_VanDyke" title="Matthew VanDyke">Matthew VanDyke</a>, a <a href="/wiki/2011_Libyan_Civil_War" class="mw-redirect" title="2011 Libyan Civil War">Libyan Civil War</a> veteran and pro-rebel news reporter.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">&#91;<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>&#93;</sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2014">2014</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: 2014"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>1 January 2014: SEA hacked <a href="/wiki/Skype" title="Skype">Skype</a>'s Facebook, Twitter and blog, posting an SEA related picture and telling users not to use Microsoft's e-mail service <a href="/wiki/Outlook.com" title="Outlook.com">Outlook.com</a> —formerly known as Hotmail—claiming that Microsoft sells user information to the government.<sup id="cite_ref-51" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-51"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>51<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>11 January 2014: SEA hacked the <a href="/wiki/Xbox" title="Xbox">Xbox</a> Support Twitter pages and directed tweets to the group's website.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>52<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>22 January 2014: SEA hacked the official <a href="/wiki/Microsoft_Office" title="Microsoft Office">Microsoft Office</a> Blog, posting several images and tweeted about the attack.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>53<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>23 January 2014: CNN's HURACAN CAMPEÓN 2014 official Twitter account showed two messages, including a photo of the Syrian Flag composed of binary code. CNN removed the Tweets within 10 minutes.<sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>54<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>55<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>3 February 2014: SEA hacked the websites of <a href="/wiki/EBay" title="EBay">eBay</a> and <a href="/wiki/PayPal" title="PayPal">PayPal</a> UK. One source reported the hackers said it was just for show and that they took no data.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>56<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>6 February 2014: SEA hacked the DNS of <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a>. Sources said the registrant contact details were restored and Facebook confirmed that no traffic to the website was hijacked, and that no users of the social network were affected.<sup id="cite_ref-57" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-57"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>57<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>14 February 2014: SEA hacked the <a href="/wiki/Forbes" title="Forbes">Forbes</a> website and their Twitter accounts.<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>58<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>26 April 2014: SEA hacked the <a href="/wiki/Information_security" title="Information security">information security</a>-related <a href="/wiki/RSA_Conference" title="RSA Conference">RSA Conference</a> website.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>59<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>18 June 2014: SEA hacked the websites of British newspapers <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sun_(United_Kingdom)" title="The Sun (United Kingdom)">The Sun (United Kingdom)</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Sunday_Times" title="The Sunday Times">The Sunday Times</a></i>.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>60<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>22 June 2014: The Reuters website was hacked a second time and showed a SEA message condemning Reuters for "publishing false articles about Syria". Hackers compromised the website, corrupting ads served by <a href="/wiki/Taboola" title="Taboola">Taboola</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>61<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>27 November 2014: SEA hacked hundreds of sites through hijacking <a href="/wiki/Gigya" title="Gigya">Gigya</a>'s comment system of prominent websites, displaying a message "You've been hacked by the Syrian Electronic Army(SEA)." Affected websites included the <i><a href="/wiki/Aberdeen_Evening_Express" class="mw-redirect" title="Aberdeen Evening Express">Aberdeen Evening Express</a></i>, Logitech, Forbes, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Independent" title="The Independent">The Independent</a></i> UK Magazine, <i><a href="/wiki/London_Evening_Standard" class="mw-redirect" title="London Evening Standard">London Evening Standard</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Telegraph</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>, the <a href="/wiki/National_Hockey_League" title="National Hockey League">National Hockey League</a>, Finishline.com, PCH.com, <a href="/wiki/Time_Out_New_York" class="mw-redirect" title="Time Out New York">Time Out New York</a> and t3.com (a tech website), stv.com, <a href="/wiki/Walmart_Canada" title="Walmart Canada">Walmart Canada</a>, <a href="/wiki/PacSun" title="PacSun">PacSun</a>, <i><a href="/wiki/Mail_Online" class="mw-redirect" title="Mail Online">Daily Mail</a></i> websites, bikeradar.com (cycling website), <a href="/wiki/SparkNotes" title="SparkNotes">SparkNotes</a>, millionshort.com, Milenio.com, Mediotiempo.com, Todobebe.com and myrecipes.com, Biz Day SA, BDlive South Africa, muscleandfitness.com, and <a href="/wiki/CBC_News" title="CBC News">CBC News</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>62<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2015">2015</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 2015"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>21 January 2015: French newspaper <i><a href="/wiki/Le_Monde" title="Le Monde">Le Monde</a></i> wrote that SEA hackers "managed to infiltrate our publishing tool before launching a denial of service".<sup id="cite_ref-63" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-63"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>63<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-reu12115_64-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-reu12115-64"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>64<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2018">2018</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 2018"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>17 May 2018: Two suspects were indicted by the United States for "conspiracy" for hacking several US websites.<sup id="cite_ref-65" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-65"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>65<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading3"><h3 id="2021">2021</h3><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: 2021"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>October 2021: <a href="/wiki/Facebook" title="Facebook">Facebook</a> discovers the presence of several fake accounts run by the SEA and its affiliated organizations. The accounts had reportedly been used to target Syrian opposition figures and human rights activists, as well as members of the <a href="/wiki/YPG" class="mw-redirect" title="YPG">YPG</a> and <a href="/wiki/White_Helmets_(Syrian_civil_war)" title="White Helmets (Syrian civil war)">White Helmets</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>66<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>67<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>
<div class="mw-heading mw-heading2"><h2 id="Legal_actions">Legal actions</h2><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Syrian_Electronic_Army&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Legal actions"><span>edit</span></a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></div>
<ul><li>10 May 2016: Syrian Electronic Army member Peter Romar was extradited from Germany to the United States to face charges brought by the Department of Justice for engaging in a "a multi-year criminal conspiracy to conduct computer intrusions against perceived detractors of President Bashar al-Assad, including media entities, the White House and foreign governments."<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>68<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>69<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li>
<li>28 September 2016: Peter Romar pled guilty to charges of helping the Syrian Electronic army extort cash from hacking victims.<sup id="cite_ref-70" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-70"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>70<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-71" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-71"><span class="cite-bracket">&#91;</span>71<span class="cite-bracket">&#93;</span></a></sup></li></ul>

Ars Technica<span class="reference-accessdate">. Retrieved <span class="nowrap">October 15,</span> 2014</span>. <q>The Syrian Computer Society acts as Syria's domain registration authority and regulates the Internet within Syria, and is also believed to be connected to Syria's state security apparatus.
